industry that accounts for nearly all of the South Asian country's export earnings.</p><p class="canvas-atom canvas-text Mb(1.0em) Mb(0)--sm Mt(0.8em)--sm" type="text" content="Factories shut their said they were now being pushed by retailers to fulfill outstanding export orders.</p><p class="canvas-atom canvas-text Mb(1.0em) Mb(0)--sm Mt(0.8em)--sm" type="text" content="&quot;We have to accept If we don't open factories, there will be economic crisis," said Bangladesh Knitwear Manufacturers and Exporters Association vice president Mohammad Hatem.</p><p class="canvas-atom canvas-text diverted to competing operations in countries like Vietnam or China, Hatem added.</p><p class="canvas-atom canvas-text Mb(1.0em) Mb(0)--sm Mt(0.8em)--sm" type="text" content="More than four million data-reactid="52">More than four million people work in thousands of garment factories across Bangladesh, which last year shipped out $35 billion of apparel to retailers such as H&amp;M, Inditex and Walmart -- second only to China.</p><p class="canvas-atom canvas-text Mb(1.0em) Mb(0)--sm Mt(0.8em)--sm" type="text" content="Hundreds of those factories had resumed operations over the weekend in the
